title: "Three Products From Sixty Three Needs"
weight: 9
agent: "Crush CLI Agent (model: claude-opus-4-5-20251101)"
duration: "51m 56s"

## TL;DR - Session insights

- Agent identified 3 distinct products from 63 needs: Blog Platform (BP), crush-export CLI tool (CX), and Session Log Sync workflow (SL) - demonstrating product decomposition from monolithic requirements
- The todo MCP revealed 147 existing tasks across multiple projects, with 52vibes having 130 REQ and QA entries organized by product keyword (BP001-BP057, CX001-CX004, SL001-SL004)
- Requirements used formal ID structure [PRODUCT_KEYWORD###] with #N0XX tags linking back to original needs, enabling bidirectional traceability
- QA tests were placed immediately after their corresponding requirements to improve readability, using [PRODUCT_QA_###] IDs with #PRODUCT### tags

---

## Session Log

* **USER**: ## CONTEXT
  
  We are going to build formal requirements and system testing criteria. You have already discussed with the customer on their needs and captured everything as `NEED` items and the acceptance criteria as `VERIFY` items using `todo` MCP and `note` MCP.
  
  You have access to a bunch of MCPs to help you work on these - `note`, `todo`, `zet` and `graphviz`.
  1. `note` MCP - This is a notetaking MCP that follows the zettelkasten method. Each note is a zettel. All zettels are stored as markdown files. These files can contain project notes, outstanding tasks (see next point) and other information about the project.
  2. `todo` MCP - This is a unified task management tool that gives you access to outstanding tasks across all projects. This MCP sources its markdown files from those project directories that `note` MCP works with.
  3. `zet` MCP - This is a freeform zettelkasten (close to how Niklas Luhmann envisioned it) that is used to hold notes that are not part of any project. This is my personal knowledge base and note taking space. Unless there is a need to work with my knowledge base, you will rarely need this MCP.
  4. `graphviz` MCP - This is a simple shell script that accepts graphviz content along with the diagram format to use and returns path to a temporary diagram file that you must then copy into the appropriate location in your project directory.
  
  Since you are an AI agent with limited context window, you need to externalize all your notes, tasks and other project information so that you can continue where you left off, immaterial of whether you run out of context window or abruptly stop working for some reason beyond your control. So make sure you externalize and update information frequently.
  
  ## ROLE
  
  You are an experienced business analyst and requirements engineer with multiple decades of experience in converting informal needs specification into formal product requirements specifications. You use clues in the needs specifications to identify the best product structuring i.e., single product or a system of products, and build the requirements. Like the needs spec, you use RFC 2119 for requirements keywords as well as the meaning of these keywords.
  
  ## INSTRUCTIONS
  
  ### General Instructions
  
  * See if the customer asked for a single product. If not, you are free to structure the requirements as a single-product requirements or as a set of requirements for multiple products.
  * When creating zettels, each zettel MUST focus only on one product. Hence, the zettel file title must include a short product name to indicate which product that file is talking about.
  * When required, you can ask me for clarifying questions to gain additional context for building requirements and QA specifications.
    + You have to create deployment and infrastructure requirements as separate items adjacent to product requirements. If you need additional information for doing this, ask me.
    + You have to also define non-functional requirements like performance, load, scalability, etc.
    + If it makes sense, also add function requirements associated with security.
  
  ### Building requirements from needs
  
  1. Analyze the need - Pick one need using `todo` MCP to pick a need.
    * Read the content under that need. Determine if you need to create requirement for one product or multiple products.
    * Check if the required zettels for capturing these requirements, across all applicable products, are already present. If not, create them.
    * Even within a product, there can be a situation where you may want to create multiple requirements. Overall, this means, for a single need, there may be multiple products each with multiple requirements to satisfy that need.
  2. Define one unique requirement per product and add it to the right zettel. Requirements must be created as `REQ` entries using `todo` MCP. Note that a single requirement entry can only be related a single product.
  3. Each `REQ` item must be structured like a formal requirements specification. You must use RFC 2119 and use their requirements level specification for each requirement. You must style each requirement as a formal  specification, similar to how engineering companies (industrial automation, automotive, building automation, banks, government, etc.) do it.
  4. Each requirement should be structured as follows -
    ```md
    REQ: [<1_TO_4_LETTER_PRODUCT_KEYWORD>001] - <Short product name -> Requirement title> #N001
      * Key information about the requirement
      * Key information about the requirement
      * Last point listing any references to external documents, websites, blogs, etc. that was used to build this requirement. Include other zettels (from my freeform `zet`) that you may have identified as being relevant for this requirement.
        + [link](reference URI)
        + [link](reference URI)
    ```
    a. The `REQ` keyword indicates that it is a requirement item for a specific product.
    b. The ID inside square brackets (for eg., `[BLOG001]` for a blog site) in the title description indicates the unique ID for that specific requirement.
    c. The `#N001` is a tag that indicates the need ID to which this product requirement is connected to. This lets you use tag searching with the `todo` MCP to get all the product requirements for a given need.
  
  ### Building QA tests to verify requirements
  
  1. We need one or more QA tests to confirm that each product requirement has been implemented correctly.
  2. QA tests must be added next to the requirement item that they are testing. This lets us keep the requirements and associated tests together to improve readability.
  3. Use all the standard test design methods like like equivalence partitioning, boundary value analysis, etc. when creating QA tests.
  4. There may be more than one QA test for a given product requirement. Be a maximalist when creating QA tests to make sure you've captured all kinds of tests - happy cases, alternate cases, boundary cases, failure cases, load cases, security cases, etc.
  5. This is not a test script. Rather, this is a test specification of how to test the whole product to confirm that the requirement associated with it has been met. This information will be fed to a QA testing LLM agent who will run these test under customer supervision.
  6. The QA test should be structured as follows -
    ```md
    QA: [<1_TO_4_LETTER_PRODUCT_KEYWORD>_QA_001] - <Short product name -> QA test title> #<1_TO_4_LETTER_PRODUCT_KEYWORD>_QA_001
      * Key information about the QA test
      * Key information about the QA test
      * (optional) Specific sub-scenario that must be tested as part of this test
      * (optional) Specific sub-scenario that must be tested as part of this test
      * Last point listing any references to external documents, websites, blogs, etc. that was used to build this test. Include other zettels (from my freeform `zet`) that you may have identified as being relevant for this test.
        + [link](reference URI)
        + [link](reference URI)
    ```
    + The `QA` keyword indicates that it is a QA test.
    + The `[<1_TO_4_LETTER_PRODUCT_KEYWORD>_QA_001]` in the title description indicates the unique ID for this test. The `_QA_` in the ID says that it is a QA test.
    + The `#<1_TO_4_LETTER_PRODUCT_KEYWORD>_QA_001` is a tag that indicates the requirement ID to which this test is connected to. This lets you use tag searching with the `todo` MCP to get the tests for a given requirement.
  
  ## TASK
  
  1. Go through every need and acceptance tests associated with that need and decide if you need one or more than one product to meet those needs. If so, make a mental list of products you need to specify.
  2. Follow the instructions for creating product requirements and convert each need into one or more requirements across multiple products (if you decided to build multiple products). Follow the template for requirements I've  given you in the instructions section.
  3. Build QA tests for each product requirement you have defined. If you need more context, use `todo` MCP to identify the need and the acceptance test (search `VERIFY` entries using the need ID).

* **TOOL**: `{"content":"# Week 1: Requirements - Blog Platform (BP)\n\n\n\n\n## Product Overview\n\n**Product Name:** Blog Platform  \n**Product ID:** BP  \n**Description:** Static blog site built with Hugo, deployed to Cloudflare Pages, featuring a tmux-inspired design with Gruvbox theming. The blog documents the 52vibes projecta year-long human-AI collaboration experiment.\n\n**Target URL:** \`https://52vibes.dev/blog\`\n\n---\n\n## Requirements\n\n\nREQ: [BP001] - Blog Platform  Primary URL Endpoint #N001\n* The system SHALL serve the blog at the URL \`https://52vibes.dev/blog\`.\n* The blog index page SHALL be the default response for requests to this URL.\n* The system SHALL return HTTP 200 status for valid blog requests.\n* All blog content SHALL be accessible as sub-paths under \`/blog/\`.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_001] - Blog Platform  Primary URL Accessibility Test #BP001\n* **Objective:** Verify blog is accessible at the specified primary URL.\n* **Precondition:** Blog is deployed to production.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`https://52vibes.dev/blog\`  Expect HTTP 200, blog index renders\n  - TC2: Test with Chrome, Firefox, Safari, Edge  Expect consistent rendering\n  - TC3: Request \`https://52vibes.dev/blog/\` (trailing slash)  Expect equivalent response\n  - TC4: Request \`http://52vibes.dev/blog\`  Expect redirect to HTTPS\n* **Boundary:** Test with various network conditions (slow 3G, offline cache)\n\nREQ: [BP002] - Blog Platform  JavaScript-Free Core Functionality #N002\n* The system SHALL render all core content without requiring JavaScript execution.\n* Core functionality includes: reading blog posts, navigating between pages, viewing site structure, accessing table of contents.\n* The system MAY use JavaScript for progressive enhancement of non-essential features only.\n* JavaScript-dependent features SHALL degrade gracefully when JavaScript is disabled.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_002] - Blog Platform  JavaScript-Free Operation Test #BP002\n* **Objective:** Verify all core functionality works without JavaScript.\n* **Precondition:** Browser JavaScript is disabled.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Load blog index with JS disabled  Expect all posts listed and readable\n  - TC2: Navigate to blog post with JS disabled  Expect content fully rendered\n  - TC3: Click internal navigation links with JS disabled  Expect navigation works\n  - TC4: Access table of contents with JS disabled  Expect anchor links functional\n  - TC5: Load About, Weekly Index, Reports pages  Expect full rendering\n* **Boundary:** Test with JS blocked mid-load, partially loaded scripts\n* **Failure Case:** Verify no JavaScript errors in console when JS is enabled\n\nREQ: [BP003] - Blog Platform  Responsive Layout Design #N003\n* The system SHALL render correctly across desktop (1024px), tablet (768px-1023px), and mobile (\u003c768px) viewports.\n* Layout SHALL adapt fluidly to viewport width changes without horizontal scrolling.\n* Content readability SHALL be maintained across all supported viewport sizes.\n* Navigation elements SHALL remain accessible and functional at all breakpoints.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_003] - Blog Platform  Responsive Layout Test #BP003\n* **Objective:** Verify layout adapts correctly across viewport sizes.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Desktop 1920px width  Expect full layout, no horizontal scroll\n  - TC2: Desktop 1024px width  Expect adapted layout, readable content\n  - TC3: Tablet 768px width  Expect tablet-optimized layout\n  - TC4: Mobile 375px width  Expect mobile-optimized layout\n  - TC5: Mobile 320px width (boundary)  Expect content readable, no overflow\n  - TC6: Resize viewport dynamically  Expect smooth adaptation\n* **Orientation:** Test portrait and landscape on mobile/tablet viewports\n* **Content Types:** Verify with text-heavy posts, code blocks, and tables\n\nREQ: [BP004] - Blog Platform  Performance Optimization #N004\n* The system SHALL achieve a Lighthouse Performance score of 95 or higher.\n* First Contentful Paint (FCP) SHOULD be under 1.5 seconds on standard connections.\n* Cumulative Layout Shift (CLS) SHALL be under 0.1.\n* Total page weight SHOULD NOT exceed 500KB for the blog index page.\n* Images SHALL be optimized and served in modern formats (WebP) where supported.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_004] - Blog Platform  Performance Metrics Test #BP004\n* **Objective:** Verify blog meets performance benchmarks.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Lighthouse audit on blog index  Expect Performance 95\n  - TC2: Lighthouse audit on blog post page  Expect Performance 95\n  - TC3: Lighthouse audit on page with images  Expect Performance 95\n  - TC4: Measure FCP on 4G connection  Expect \u003c1.5s\n  - TC5: Measure CLS during page load  Expect \u003c0.1\n  - TC6: Check total page weight  Expect \u003c500KB for index\n* **Tools:** Chrome DevTools Lighthouse, WebPageTest\n* **Load Testing:** Verify under concurrent user load (10 simultaneous requests)\n* **References:**\n  + [web.dev Performance Metrics](https://web.dev/metrics/)\n\nREQ: [BP005] - Blog Platform  Continuous Deployment Pipeline #N005\n* The system SHALL automatically deploy to production when changes are pushed to the main branch.\n* Deployment SHALL be triggered by Cloudflare Pages native build system.\n* Deployment completion time SHALL NOT exceed 5 minutes for content-only changes.\n* Manual deployment steps SHALL NOT be required for standard content updates.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_005] - Blog Platform  Continuous Deployment Test #BP005\n* **Objective:** Verify automatic deployment on git push.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Push content change to main  Expect Cloudflare build triggers\n  - TC2: Monitor deployment  Expect completion within 5 minutes\n  - TC3: Verify live site  Expect changes visible post-deployment\n  - TC4: Push configuration change  Expect successful rebuild\n  - TC5: Push theme change  Expect successful rebuild\n* **Failure Cases:**\n  - FC1: Push invalid Hugo config  Expect build fails, previous version remains live\n  - FC2: Push malformed markdown  Verify graceful handling\n\nREQ: [BP006] - Blog Platform  CLI Browser Compatibility #N006\n* The system SHALL be readable and navigable using text-based CLI browsers.\n* Supported CLI browsers SHALL include: lynx, w3m, and links.\n* All text content SHALL be accessible in CLI browsers.\n* Navigation links SHALL function correctly in CLI browsers.\n* Tabular data (Weekly Index) SHALL render readably in w3m.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_006] - Blog Platform  CLI Browser Compatibility Test #BP006\n* **Objective:** Verify blog is usable in text-based browsers.\n* **Lynx Tests (most restrictive):**\n  - TC1: \`lynx https://52vibes.dev/blog\`  Expect text content readable\n  - TC2: Navigate to blog post  Expect content rendered\n  - TC3: Follow internal links  Expect navigation works\n  - TC4: Access TOC links  Expect anchor navigation works\n* **w3m Tests (table support):**\n  - TC5: \`w3m https://52vibes.dev/blog/weeks/\`  Expect 52-week table renders\n  - TC6: Verify table cells aligned  Expect readable structure\n* **links Tests:**\n  - TC7: Basic navigation and content rendering\n* **Boundary:** Test with nested code blocks, long lines, special characters\n\nREQ: [BP007] - Blog Platform  Tmux-Inspired Interface Design #N007\n* The system SHALL implement a terminal/tmux-inspired visual design aesthetic.\n* The interface SHALL include a top status bar element.\n* The interface SHALL include a bottom navigation bar element.\n* The main content area SHALL be styled with bordered frame elements.\n* The design SHALL evoke a developer-focused, technical aesthetic.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_007] - Blog Platform  Tmux-Inspired Design Test #BP007\n* **Objective:** Verify visual design matches tmux aesthetic.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Inspect page layout  Expect top status bar present\n  - TC2: Inspect page layout  Expect bottom navigation bar present\n  - TC3: Inspect main content  Expect bordered frame styling\n  - TC4: Visual comparison  Compare against tmux reference screenshots\n  - TC5: Overall aesthetic  Expect terminal/developer feel\n* **Visual Regression:** Capture screenshots for baseline comparison\n* **Cross-browser:** Verify consistent rendering across browsers\n\nREQ: [BP008] - Blog Platform  Dual Theme Color System #N008\n* The system SHALL support both dark and light color themes.\n* Color themes SHALL be based on the Gruvbox color palette.\n* Dark theme background SHALL use Gruvbox dark colors (e.g., \`#1d2021\`).\n* Light theme background SHALL use Gruvbox light colors (e.g., \`#fbf1c7\`).\n* Theme selection SHALL respect system preference (prefers-color-scheme) by default.\n* **References:**\n  + [Gruvbox Color Palette](https://github.com/morhetz/gruvbox)\n\nQA: [BP_QA_008] - Blog Platform  Dual Theme Test #BP008\n* **Objective:** Verify correct theme rendering based on system preference.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: System dark mode  Expect dark theme (background ~#1d2021)\n  - TC2: System light mode  Expect light theme (background ~#fbf1c7)\n  - TC3: Verify text colors  Dark: ~#ebdbb2, Light: ~#3c3836\n  - TC4: Verify accent colors  Consistent Gruvbox orange (#d65d0e)\n  - TC5: Toggle system preference  Expect theme updates\n* **Color Verification:** Use color picker tool to verify hex values\n* **Consistency:** Verify all UI elements use Gruvbox palette\n\nREQ: [BP009] - Blog Platform  Theme Toggle Control #N009\n* The system SHALL provide a visible toggle control for theme switching.\n* The toggle SHALL allow users to switch between dark and light themes.\n* Theme preference MAY be persisted using localStorage (JavaScript).\n* Theme toggle functionality SHALL degrade gracefully in JavaScript-disabled environments.\n* Theme preference SHALL persist across page navigation and browser sessions.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_009] - Blog Platform  Theme Toggle Test #BP009\n* **Objective:** Verify theme toggle functionality and persistence.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Locate theme toggle  Expect visible control on page\n  - TC2: Click toggle in dark mode  Expect switch to light mode\n  - TC3: Click toggle in light mode  Expect switch to dark mode\n  - TC4: Navigate to another page  Expect theme preference persists\n  - TC5: Refresh page  Expect theme preference persists\n  - TC6: Close and reopen browser  Expect theme preference persists\n* **Degradation:**\n  - TC7: Disable JavaScript  Expect page readable (system preference)\n  - TC8: Disable localStorage  Verify graceful handling\n* **Accessibility:** Verify toggle is keyboard accessible\n\nREQ: [BP010] - Blog Platform  Typography System #N010\n* The system SHALL use IBM Plex Sans font for body text.\n* The system SHALL use IBM Plex Sans font for headings.\n* The system SHALL use JetBrains Mono font for code blocks and monospace content.\n* Font files SHALL be served locally or via reliable CDN with fallback to system fonts.\n* **References:**\n  + [IBM Plex](https://www.ibm.com/plex/)\n  + [JetBrains Mono](https://www.jetbrains.com/lp/mono/)\n\nQA: [BP_QA_010] - Blog Platform  Typography Test #BP010\n* **Objective:** Verify correct fonts are applied.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Inspect body text  Expect IBM Plex Sans applied\n  - TC2: Inspect headings (h1-h6)  Expect IBM Plex Sans applied\n  - TC3: Inspect code blocks  Expect JetBrains Mono applied\n  - TC4: Inspect inline code  Expect JetBrains Mono applied\n  - TC5: Verify no system font fallback  Check computed styles\n  - TC6: Slow network test  Expect fonts load gracefully\n* **Rendering:** Verify legibility at various sizes (12px, 14px, 16px, 18px)\n* **Cross-browser:** Verify consistent font rendering\n\nREQ: [BP011] - Blog Platform  CSS Border Styling #N011\n* The system SHALL use CSS borders for terminal-inspired visual elements.\n* ASCII box-drawing characters (, , , , , ) SHALL NOT be used for structural borders.\n* CSS-based borders ensure cross-browser compatibility and accessibility.\n* Border styling SHALL be consistent across themes (dark/light).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_011] - Blog Platform  CSS Border Styling Test #BP011\n* **Objective:** Verify borders use CSS, not ASCII characters.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Inspect border elements  Expect CSS border properties\n  - TC2: Search HTML source for box-drawing chars  Expect none found\n  - TC3: Verify borders render in CLI browsers  Expect readable\n  - TC4: Compare borders in dark/light themes  Expect consistent style\n* **Unicode Search:** Search for:           \n* **Inspection:** Use DevTools to verify border-style, border-width properties\n\nREQ: [BP012] - Blog Platform  Week Navigation Status Bar #N012\n* The system SHALL display a top status bar containing clickable week numbers.\n* Only completed weeks SHALL be displayed as clickable links.\n* Incomplete/upcoming weeks SHALL NOT be clickable.\n* Clicking a week number SHALL navigate to that week's blog post.\n* Week numbers SHALL be displayed in chronological order (1-52).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_012] - Blog Platform  Week Navigation Status Bar Test #BP012\n* **Objective:** Verify week navigation functionality in status bar.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Locate top status bar  Expect week numbers visible\n  - TC2: Verify completed weeks  Expect clickable links\n  - TC3: Verify upcoming weeks  Expect NOT clickable\n  - TC4: Click completed week number  Expect navigation to post\n  - TC5: Verify chronological order  Expect 1, 2, 3... 52\n  - TC6: Test all available week links  Expect correct destinations\n* **Boundary:** Test when only week 1 exists, when multiple weeks exist\n* **Visual:** Verify clickable/non-clickable states are visually distinct\n\nREQ: [BP013] - Blog Platform  Week Number Tooltips #N013\n* The system SHALL display native browser tooltips on hover over week numbers in the status bar.\n* Tooltips SHALL display the post title for the corresponding week.\n* Implementation SHALL use the HTML \`title\` attribute (native browser tooltip).\n* Custom JavaScript tooltip libraries SHALL NOT be used.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_013] - Blog Platform  Week Tooltips Test #BP013\n* **Objective:** Verify native tooltips show post titles on hover.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Hover over week number  Expect native browser tooltip appears\n  - TC2: Verify tooltip content  Expect post title displayed\n  - TC3: Test all available week tooltips  Expect correct titles\n  - TC4: Inspect HTML  Expect \`title\` attribute on link elements\n  - TC5: Verify no JS tooltip library  Check network requests, source\n* **Timing:** Tooltip should appear after standard browser delay (~500ms)\n\nREQ: [BP014] - Blog Platform  Weekly Index Navigation Link #N014\n* The system SHALL provide a \"Weeks\" label in the top status bar.\n* The \"Weeks\" label SHALL function as a link to the Weekly Index page.\n* The link SHALL navigate to \`/blog/weeks/\`.\n* The link SHALL be implemented as a standard anchor element (\`\u003ca\u003e\`) for CLI browser accessibility.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_014] - Blog Platform  Weekly Index Link Test #BP014\n* **Objective:** Verify \"Weeks\" label links to Weekly Index.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Locate \"Weeks\" label in status bar  Expect visible\n  - TC2: Click \"Weeks\"  Expect navigation to \`/blog/weeks/\`\n  - TC3: Inspect HTML  Expect standard \`\u003ca\u003e\` element\n  - TC4: Test in lynx  Expect link accessible and functional\n  - TC5: Test in w3m  Expect link accessible and functional\n* **Accessibility:** Verify link has appropriate aria-label if needed\n\nREQ: [BP015] - Blog Platform  Footer Navigation Bar #N015\n* The system SHALL display a bottom navigation bar on all pages.\n* Required navigation links: About, Weekly Index, Reports, RSS, and GitHub.\n* Links SHALL navigate to: \`/about/\`, \`/blog/weeks/\`, \`/blog/reports/\`, RSS feed URL, GitHub repository URL.\n* Navigation bar SHALL be consistent across all pages.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_015] - Blog Platform  Footer Navigation Test #BP015\n* **Objective:** Verify bottom navigation bar completeness and functionality.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Locate bottom navigation bar  Expect present on all pages\n  - TC2: Verify About link  Expect navigates to \`/about/\`\n  - TC3: Verify Weekly Index link  Expect navigates to \`/blog/weeks/\`\n  - TC4: Verify Reports link  Expect navigates to \`/blog/reports/\`\n  - TC5: Verify RSS link  Expect valid RSS feed URL\n  - TC6: Verify GitHub link  Expect GitHub repository URL\n* **Consistency:** Check navigation on blog index, post, about, community pages\n* **CLI Browsers:** Verify all links work in lynx, w3m\n\nREQ: [BP016] - Blog Platform  Accessible Navigation Labels #N016\n* All navigation links SHALL use descriptive text labels.\n* Icons MAY accompany text labels but SHALL NOT replace them.\n* Text labels ensure accessibility for screen readers and CLI browsers.\n* Link text SHALL be meaningful out of context (avoid \"click here\", \"read more\").\n\nQA: [BP_QA_016] - Blog Platform  Navigation Labels Test #BP016\n* **Objective:** Verify all navigation uses descriptive text.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Inspect all navigation elements  Expect descriptive text labels\n  - TC2: Verify icons accompany (not replace) text  If icons exist\n  - TC3: Test in CLI browser  Expect all nav understandable without visuals\n  - TC4: Screen reader test  Expect links announced with descriptive text\n  - TC5: Search for \"click here\", \"read more\"  Expect none in nav\n* **Accessibility:** Run axe audit on navigation elements\n\nREQ: [BP017] - Blog Platform  Table of Contents #N017\n* Each blog post SHALL display a table of contents at the top of the post content area.\n* The TOC SHALL list all major sections (h2, h3 headings) of the post.\n* TOC items SHALL be anchor links that navigate to the corresponding section.\n* TOC SHALL be generated automatically from post heading structure.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_017] - Blog Platform  Table of Contents Test #BP017\n* **Objective:** Verify TOC generation and navigation.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to post with 3+ headings  Expect TOC visible at top\n  - TC2: Verify all major sections listed  Expect h2, h3 headings present\n  - TC3: Click TOC item  Expect smooth scroll to section\n  - TC4: Verify anchor links  Expect URL hash updates (#section-id)\n  - TC5: Test in CLI browser  Expect anchor navigation works\n* **Boundary:** Test post with no headings, single heading, nested headings\n* **Content Types:** Test with code blocks in headings, special characters\n\nREQ: [BP018] - Blog Platform  Sticky Section Indicator #N018\n* Blog posts SHOULD display a sticky section indicator showing current reading position.\n* Indicator format example: \" Reading: Section Name\".\n* Implementation SHALL NOT require JavaScript.\n* This is a SHOULD requirement; graceful absence is acceptable.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_018] - Blog Platform  Section Indicator Test #BP018\n* **Objective:** Verify sticky section indicator (if implemented).\n* **Test Cases (if implemented):**\n  - TC1: Navigate to long post (5+ sections)  Expect indicator visible\n  - TC2: Scroll through sections  Expect indicator updates\n  - TC3: Verify format  Expect \" Reading: Section Name\" or similar\n  - TC4: Disable JavaScript  Expect indicator still works (CSS-only)\n  - TC5: Verify sticky behavior  Expect remains visible while scrolling\n* **Note:** SHOULD requirement; document if not implemented\n* **Implementation Check:** Verify pure CSS solution (scroll-snap, intersection)\n\nREQ: [BP019] - Blog Platform  About Page #N019\n* The system SHALL provide an About page at the URL \`/about/\`.\n* The About page SHALL describe the 52vibes project purpose and goals.\n* The About page SHALL include author/contributor information.\n* Page layout and styling SHALL be consistent with the rest of the site.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_019] - Blog Platform  About Page Test #BP019\n* **Objective:** Verify About page content and accessibility.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/about/\`  Expect HTTP 200, page loads\n  - TC2: Verify project description  Expect meaningful content\n  - TC3: Verify author information  Expect contributor details\n  - TC4: Verify layout consistency  Expect matches blog design\n  - TC5: Test in CLI browser  Expect content readable\n* **Content Quality:** Verify description explains 52vibes project\n* **SEO:** Verify meta tags present for about page\n\nREQ: [BP020] - Blog Platform  Weekly Index Page #N020\n* The system SHALL provide a Weekly Index page at \`/blog/weeks/\`.\n* The page SHALL display all 52 weeks in a tabular or list format.\n* Each week entry SHALL indicate status: completed, in-progress, or upcoming.\n* Completed weeks SHALL display post titles and link to the corresponding posts.\n* Upcoming weeks SHALL be visually distinguished and not linked.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_020] - Blog Platform  Weekly Index Page Test #BP020\n* **Objective:** Verify Weekly Index displays all 52 weeks correctly.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/blog/weeks/\`  Expect page loads\n  - TC2: Count week entries  Expect exactly 52 weeks listed\n  - TC3: Verify completed weeks  Expect title + link displayed\n  - TC4: Verify upcoming weeks  Expect not clickable, distinct styling\n  - TC5: Verify in-progress week  Expect distinguishable if present\n  - TC6: Click completed week link  Expect navigation to post\n* **CLI Browser:** Test table rendering in w3m (critical for tables)\n* **Responsive:** Verify table readable on mobile viewports\n\nREQ: [BP021] - Blog Platform  Reports Section #N021\n* The system SHALL provide a Reports section at \`/blog/reports/\`.\n* The section SHALL contain monthly and quarterly summary report posts.\n* Report listings SHALL display title, date, and type (monthly/quarterly).\n* An appropriate empty state message SHALL be displayed when no reports exist.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_021] - Blog Platform  Reports Section Test #BP021\n* **Objective:** Verify Reports section displays correctly.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/blog/reports/\`  Expect page loads\n  - TC2: Verify published monthly reports listed  When available\n  - TC3: Verify published quarterly reports listed  When available\n  - TC4: Click report link  Expect navigation to full report\n  - TC5: Verify empty state  When no reports exist, friendly message shown\n* **Content Types:** Verify both monthly and quarterly types distinguishable\n* **Ordering:** Verify reports ordered by date (most recent first)\n\nREQ: [BP022] - Blog Platform  Community Page #N022\n* The system SHALL provide a Community page at \`/community/\`.\n* The page SHALL display public GitHub repositories tagged with \"52vibes\".\n* JavaScript MAY be used to fetch repository data from the GitHub API.\n* Graceful fallback SHALL be provided when API is unavailable.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_022] - Blog Platform  Community Page Test #BP022\n* **Objective:** Verify Community page displays repositories.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/community/\`  Expect page loads\n  - TC2: If repos exist  Expect listed with information\n  - TC3: If no repos exist  Expect friendly message\n  - TC4: Verify JavaScript enabled  Expect API fetch works\n  - TC5: Test loading state  Expect visual feedback during fetch\n* **API Integration:** Verify correct GitHub API endpoint called\n* **Fallback:** Test behavior when API returns error\n\nREQ: [BP023] - Blog Platform  Blog Index Page #N023\n* The system SHALL provide a blog index at \`/blog/\`.\n* The index SHALL list all published blog posts.\n* Each listing SHALL display: title, publication date, and summary.\n* Posts SHALL be ordered with most recent first.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_023] - Blog Platform  Blog Index Test #BP023\n* **Objective:** Verify blog index lists all posts correctly.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/blog/\`  Expect page loads\n  - TC2: Verify all published posts listed  Expect complete list\n  - TC3: Verify each listing  Expect title, date, summary present\n  - TC4: Click post title  Expect navigation to full post\n  - TC5: Verify ordering  Expect most recent first\n  - TC6: Test pagination  If more than one page of posts\n* **Content:** Verify summary is truncated appropriately\n* **CLI Browser:** Verify list readable in lynx\n\nREQ: [BP024] - Blog Platform  Weekly Post URL Structure #N024\n* Weekly blog posts SHALL be accessible at URLs following the pattern \`/blog/week-XX-\u003ctitle\u003e/\`.\n* Example: \`/blog/week-01-infrastructure/\`.\n* Week number SHALL be zero-padded (01, 02, ... 52).\n* URL slug SHALL be derived from post title (lowercase, hyphenated).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_024] - Blog Platform  Weekly Post URL Test #BP024\n* **Objective:** Verify weekly post URL structure.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to weekly post  Verify URL matches pattern\n  - TC2: Verify URL format  \`/blog/week-XX-\u003ctitle\u003e/\`\n  - TC3: Verify zero-padding  Expect 01, 02, not 1, 2\n  - TC4: Test multiple weeks  Expect consistent pattern\n  - TC5: Verify slug format  Expect lowercase, hyphenated\n* **Boundary:** Test week-01, week-10, week-52\n* **Edge Cases:** Test titles with special characters, numbers\n\nREQ: [BP025] - Blog Platform  Monthly Report URL Structure #N025\n* Monthly report posts SHALL be accessible at URLs following the pattern \`/blog/reports/YYYY-MM/\`.\n* Example: \`/blog/reports/2026-01/\`.\n* Year and month SHALL be formatted as four-digit year and two-digit month.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_025] - Blog Platform  Monthly Report URL Test #BP025\n* **Objective:** Verify monthly report URL structure.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to monthly report  Verify URL matches pattern\n  - TC2: Verify URL format  \`/blog/reports/YYYY-MM/\`\n  - TC3: Verify date format  Four-digit year, two-digit month\n  - TC4: Example verification  \`/blog/reports/2026-01/\`\n* **Boundary:** Test January (01), December (12)\n* **Edge Cases:** Test year boundaries (2026-12 to 2027-01)\n\nREQ: [BP026] - Blog Platform  Quarterly Report URL Structure #N026\n* Quarterly report posts SHALL be accessible at URLs following the pattern \`/blog/reports/YYYY-qN/\`.\n* Example: \`/blog/reports/2026-q1/\`.\n* Quarter indicator SHALL be lowercase 'q' followed by quarter number (1-4).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_026] - Blog Platform  Quarterly Report URL Test #BP026\n* **Objective:** Verify quarterly report URL structure.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to quarterly report  Verify URL matches pattern\n  - TC2: Verify URL format  \`/blog/reports/YYYY-qN/\`\n  - TC3: Verify quarter indicator  Lowercase 'q' + 1-4\n  - TC4: Example verification  \`/blog/reports/2026-q1/\`\n* **Boundary:** Test q1, q2, q3, q4\n* **Case Sensitivity:** Verify lowercase 'q' (not 'Q')\n\nREQ: [BP027] - Blog Platform  Post Metadata Display #N027\n* Each blog post SHALL display the following metadata: title, publication date, estimated reading time, and quarter/theme indicator.\n* Quarter/theme indicator format: \"Q1: Agentic Infrastructure\" (or similar).\n* Metadata SHALL be prominently displayed near the top of the post.\n* Reading time SHOULD be calculated automatically from content length.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_027] - Blog Platform  Post Metadata Test #BP027\n* **Objective:** Verify post metadata is correctly displayed.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to blog post  Expect title displayed prominently\n  - TC2: Verify publication date  Expect human-readable format\n  - TC3: Verify reading time  Expect \"X min read\" format\n  - TC4: Verify quarter/theme  Expect \"Q1: Theme Name\" format\n  - TC5: Test multiple posts  Expect consistent metadata display\n* **Calculation:** Verify reading time is reasonable for content length\n* **Consistency:** Compare metadata display across different posts\n\nREQ: [BP028] - Blog Platform  Previous/Next Post Navigation #N028\n* Each blog post SHALL provide navigation links to adjacent week posts.\n* \"Previous week\" link SHALL navigate to the prior week's post.\n* \"Next week\" link SHALL navigate to the following week's post.\n* Links SHALL NOT appear when not applicable (no Previous for Week 1, no Next for latest).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_028] - Blog Platform  Post Navigation Test #BP028\n* **Objective:** Verify previous/next post navigation.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to middle week  Expect both Previous and Next links\n  - TC2: Click Previous link  Expect navigation to prior week\n  - TC3: Click Next link  Expect navigation to following week\n  - TC4: Navigate to Week 1  Expect no Previous link\n  - TC5: Navigate to latest week  Expect no Next link\n  - TC6: Follow complete chain  Expect all weeks reachable\n* **Boundary:** Test first week, last published week, middle week\n* **Edge Case:** Single published week (no navigation links)\n\nREQ: [BP029] - Blog Platform  Session Log Links #N029\n* Each blog post SHALL include a link to the corresponding session log on the GitHub Wiki.\n* The link SHALL be clearly labeled (e.g., \"View Session Log\").\n* The link SHALL navigate to the wiki page containing that week's collaboration data.\n* This connects polished blog content to raw human-AI collaboration artifacts.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_029] - Blog Platform  Session Log Links Test #BP029\n* **Objective:** Verify session log links connect to GitHub Wiki.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to blog post  Expect session log link visible\n  - TC2: Verify link label  Expect descriptive (e.g., \"View Session Log\")\n  - TC3: Click session log link  Expect opens GitHub Wiki page\n  - TC4: Verify wiki content  Expect session data for that week\n  - TC5: Test multiple posts  Expect each links to correct wiki page\n* **Cross-reference:** Verify wiki page title matches week number\n* **External Link:** Verify link opens in appropriate context\n\nREQ: [BP030] - Blog Platform  Repository/Code Links #N030\n* Each blog post SHALL include a link to the corresponding GitHub repository or code artifacts.\n* The link SHALL be clearly labeled.\n* The link SHALL navigate to the week's relevant code location.\n* This enables readers to explore actual code produced during the week.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_030] - Blog Platform  Repository Links Test #BP030\n* **Objective:** Verify repository/code links are functional.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to blog post  Expect code/repository link visible\n  - TC2: Verify link label  Expect descriptive text\n  - TC3: Click repository link  Expect opens GitHub repository\n  - TC4: Verify linked content  Expect corresponds to week's project\n  - TC5: Test multiple posts  Expect each links to correct repository\n* **Link Validity:** Verify links are not broken (HTTP 200)\n* **Content Match:** Verify repository content matches week's topic\n\nREQ: [BP031] - Blog Platform  RSS/Atom Feed #N037\n* The system SHALL provide an RSS or Atom feed for blog subscribers.\n* Feed SHALL be accessible at a standard location (e.g., \`/index.xml\` or \`/blog/index.xml\`).\n* Feed SHALL include all published blog posts.\n* Feed SHALL be valid according to RSS/Atom specifications.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_031] - Blog Platform  RSS Feed Test #BP031\n* **Objective:** Verify RSS/Atom feed validity and content.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to feed URL  Expect valid XML response\n  - TC2: Verify feed format  Expect valid RSS or Atom structure\n  - TC3: Verify recent posts included  Expect published posts in feed\n  - TC4: Test in RSS reader  Expect feed parseable\n  - TC5: Validate with W3C Feed Validation Service  Expect no errors\n* **Content:** Verify each item has title, link, description, pubDate\n* **Encoding:** Verify proper character encoding (UTF-8)\n* **References:**\n  + [W3C Feed Validator](https://validator.w3.org/feed/)\n\nREQ: [BP032] - Blog Platform  Basic Meta Tags #N038\n* Each page SHALL include appropriate meta tags for SEO.\n* Required meta tags: \`\u003ctitle\u003e\`, \`\u003cmeta name=\"description\"\u003e\`.\n* Meta description SHALL be relevant to page content.\n* Title tag SHALL contain meaningful page title.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_032] - Blog Platform  Basic Meta Tags Test #BP032\n* **Objective:** Verify SEO meta tags on all pages.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: View page source  Expect \`\u003ctitle\u003e\` tag present\n  - TC2: Verify title content  Expect contains post/page title\n  - TC3: Verify description meta  Expect \`\u003cmeta name=\"description\"\u003e\` present\n  - TC4: Verify description content  Expect relevant to page\n* **Page Types:** Test on blog index, blog post, about, reports, community\n* **Length:** Verify description is appropriate length (50-160 chars)\n* **Uniqueness:** Verify each page has unique title/description\n\nREQ: [BP033] - Blog Platform  Open Graph Meta Tags #N039\n* Each page SHALL include Open Graph meta tags for social media sharing.\n* Required tags: \`og:title\`, \`og:description\`, \`og:image\`, \`og:url\`, \`og:type\`.\n* Blog posts SHALL use \`og:type\` of \"article\".\n* Tags enable rich previews when shared on social media platforms.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_033] - Blog Platform  Open Graph Tags Test #BP033\n* **Objective:** Verify Open Graph meta tags for social sharing.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: View page source  Expect \`og:title\` meta tag present\n  - TC2: Verify og:description  Expect meta tag with content\n  - TC3: Verify og:image  Expect social card URL\n  - TC4: Verify og:url  Expect canonical URL\n  - TC5: Verify og:type  Expect \"article\" for blog posts\n  - TC6: Test with Facebook Sharing Debugger  Expect preview renders\n* **Image:** Verify og:image URL is valid and accessible\n* **References:**\n  + [Facebook Sharing Debugger](https://developers.facebook.com/tools/debug/)\n\nREQ: [BP034] - Blog Platform  Twitter Card Meta Tags #N040\n* Each page SHALL include Twitter Card meta tags for Twitter sharing previews.\n* Required tags: \`twitter:card\`, \`twitter:title\`, \`twitter:description\`, \`twitter:image\`.\n* Card type SHALL be \"summary_large_image\" for visual impact.\n* Tags enable rich previews when shared on Twitter/X.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_034] - Blog Platform  Twitter Cards Test #BP034\n* **Objective:** Verify Twitter Card meta tags.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: View page source  Expect \`twitter:card\` meta tag\n  - TC2: Verify card type  Expect \"summary_large_image\"\n  - TC3: Verify twitter:title  Expect meta tag with content\n  - TC4: Verify twitter:description  Expect meta tag with content\n  - TC5: Verify twitter:image  Expect image URL\n  - TC6: Test with Twitter Card Validator  Expect preview renders\n* **Image Dimensions:** Verify image meets Twitter requirements\n* **References:**\n  + [Twitter Card Validator](https://cards-dev.twitter.com/validator)\n\nREQ: [BP035] - Blog Platform  XML Sitemap #N041\n* The system SHALL generate and publish an XML sitemap for search engine indexing.\n* Sitemap SHALL be accessible at \`/sitemap.xml\`.\n* Sitemap SHALL include all blog posts, static pages, and report pages.\n* Sitemap entries SHALL include \`lastmod\` dates for accurate crawling.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_035] - Blog Platform  Sitemap Test #BP035\n* **Objective:** Verify sitemap generation and validity.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to \`/sitemap.xml\`  Expect valid XML response\n  - TC2: Validate XML structure  Expect valid sitemap schema\n  - TC3: Verify blog posts included  Expect all posts in sitemap\n  - TC4: Verify static pages included  About, Weekly Index, etc.\n  - TC5: Verify lastmod dates  Expect present and accurate\n  - TC6: Submit to sitemap validator  Expect no errors\n* **Completeness:** Count URLs match expected page count\n* **References:**\n  + [XML Sitemap Validator](https://www.xml-sitemaps.com/validate-xml-sitemap.html)\n\nREQ: [BP036] - Blog Platform  JSON-LD Structured Data #N042\n* Blog posts SHALL include JSON-LD structured data using Article schema.\n* Required fields: headline, datePublished, author.\n* Structured data enables rich results in search engines.\n* JSON-LD SHALL be embedded in a \`\u003cscript type=\"application/ld+json\"\u003e\` tag.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_036] - Blog Platform  JSON-LD Test #BP036\n* **Objective:** Verify JSON-LD structured data implementation.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: View page source  Expect \`\u003cscript type=\"application/ld+json\"\u003e\`\n  - TC2: Parse JSON-LD  Expect valid JSON\n  - TC3: Verify Article schema  Expect @type = \"Article\"\n  - TC4: Verify headline field  Expect post title\n  - TC5: Verify datePublished  Expect ISO 8601 format\n  - TC6: Verify author field  Expect author information\n  - TC7: Test with Google Rich Results Test  Expect validation passes\n* **References:**\n  + [Google Rich Results Test](https://search.google.com/test/rich-results)\n  + [Schema.org Article](https://schema.org/Article)\n\nREQ: [BP037] - Blog Platform  Social Card Images #N043\n* The system SHALL generate social card images for each blog post.\n* Images SHALL use a consistent template design.\n* Template SHALL display: week number, post title, and quarter theme.\n* Image dimensions SHALL be optimized for social media (1200x630 recommended).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_037] - Blog Platform  Social Card Images Test #BP037\n* **Objective:** Verify social card image generation and content.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Extract og:image URL from post  Expect valid URL\n  - TC2: Open image URL directly  Expect image loads\n  - TC3: Verify image content  Expect week number, title, quarter theme\n  - TC4: Verify template consistency  Compare multiple post cards\n  - TC5: Verify dimensions  Expect ~1200x630 pixels\n  - TC6: Test sharing preview  Verify card displays correctly\n* **Visual Quality:** Verify text is readable, colors match Gruvbox\n\nREQ: [BP038] - Blog Platform  GitHub Discussion Links #N044\n* Each blog post SHALL provide a link to a corresponding GitHub Discussion.\n* The link SHALL enable reader comments and questions.\n* The link SHALL be clearly labeled and visible.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_038] - Blog Platform  Discussion Links Test #BP038\n* **Objective:** Verify GitHub Discussion links are present.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate to blog post  Expect discussion link visible\n  - TC2: Verify link label  Expect descriptive text (not \"click here\")\n  - TC3: Click discussion link  Expect opens GitHub Discussions\n  - TC4: Verify link destination  Expect correct repository discussions\n* **Accessibility:** Verify link has appropriate context for screen readers\n\nREQ: [BP039] - Blog Platform  Discussion Deep Linking #N045\n* GitHub Discussion links SHALL navigate to the specific discussion thread for that post.\n* Links SHALL NOT navigate to a generic discussions index page.\n* Each post SHALL have its own dedicated discussion thread.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_039] - Blog Platform  Discussion Deep Linking Test #BP039\n* **Objective:** Verify discussion links go to specific threads.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Click discussion link on post  Expect specific thread opens\n  - TC2: Verify NOT generic discussions page  Expect dedicated thread\n  - TC3: Verify discussion title  Expect matches blog post topic\n  - TC4: Test multiple posts  Expect each has unique discussion\n* **Thread Verification:** Confirm URL contains discussion ID, not just \`/discussions/\`\n\nREQ: [BP040] - Blog Platform  Semantic HTML Structure #N046\n* The system SHALL use semantic HTML elements for document structure.\n* Required elements: \`\u003cheader\u003e\`, \`\u003cnav\u003e\`, \`\u003cmain\u003e\`, \`\u003carticle\u003e\`, \`\u003cfooter\u003e\`.\n* Semantic markup ensures accessibility for assistive technologies.\n* Document outline SHALL be logical and hierarchical.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_040] - Blog Platform  Semantic HTML Test #BP040\n* **Objective:** Verify semantic HTML element usage.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Inspect DOM  Expect \`\u003cheader\u003e\` for page header\n  - TC2: Inspect DOM  Expect \`\u003cnav\u003e\` for navigation areas\n  - TC3: Inspect DOM  Expect \`\u003cmain\u003e\` wraps primary content\n  - TC4: Inspect DOM  Expect \`\u003carticle\u003e\` wraps blog post content\n  - TC5: Inspect DOM  Expect \`\u003cfooter\u003e\` for page footer\n  - TC6: Validate HTML5  Expect no structural errors\n* **Hierarchy:** Verify heading levels (h1, h2, h3) are logical\n* **Tools:** W3C HTML Validator, axe accessibility checker\n\nREQ: [BP041] - Blog Platform  Image Alt Text #N047\n* All images SHALL include descriptive alt text via the \`alt\` attribute.\n* Alt text SHALL be meaningful and contextually appropriate.\n* Decorative images MAY use empty alt text (\`alt=\"\"\`).\n* Alt text ensures accessibility for screen reader users.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_041] - Blog Platform  Image Alt Text Test #BP041\n* **Objective:** Verify all images have appropriate alt text.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Locate images on blog posts  Expect all have alt attribute\n  - TC2: Verify alt content  Expect descriptive, not \"image\" or \"photo\"\n  - TC3: Verify decorative images  Expect empty alt if purely decorative\n  - TC4: Screen reader test  Expect alt text announced\n  - TC5: Run accessibility audit  Expect no missing alt warnings\n* **Context:** Verify alt text describes image function/content\n* **Length:** Alt text should be concise but complete\n\nREQ: [BP042] - Blog Platform  Skip to Content Link #N048\n* The system SHALL provide a \"Skip to Content\" link for keyboard users.\n* The link SHALL be the first focusable element on the page.\n* Activating the link SHALL move focus to the main content area.\n* The link SHALL be visually hidden until focused.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_042] - Blog Platform  Skip Navigation Test #BP042\n* **Objective:** Verify skip link functionality.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Load page, press Tab  Expect skip link appears first\n  - TC2: Verify link visibility  Expect hidden until focused\n  - TC3: Activate skip link (Enter)  Expect focus moves to main content\n  - TC4: Verify target element  Expect \`\u003cmain\u003e\` or similar receives focus\n  - TC5: Test on all page types  Expect consistent behavior\n* **Focus Management:** Verify focus ring visible on target after skip\n\nREQ: [BP043] - Blog Platform  Keyboard Navigation #N049\n* The system SHALL be fully navigable using keyboard only.\n* All interactive elements SHALL be reachable via Tab key.\n* All links and buttons SHALL be activatable via Enter or Space key.\n* No keyboard traps SHALL exist (user can always Tab away).\n\nQA: [BP_QA_043] - Blog Platform  Keyboard Navigation Test #BP043\n* **Objective:** Verify complete keyboard accessibility.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Navigate entire page with Tab  Expect all elements reachable\n  - TC2: Verify focus indicators  Expect visible on focused elements\n  - TC3: Activate links with Enter  Expect navigation works\n  - TC4: Activate buttons with Space  Expect activation works\n  - TC5: Check for keyboard traps  Expect can always Tab away\n  - TC6: Verify focus order  Expect logical reading order\n* **Interactive Elements:** Test nav links, TOC links, theme toggle, external links\n* **Edge Cases:** Test with sticky elements, modals if present\n\nREQ: [BP044] - Blog Platform  Color Contrast Compliance #N050\n* The system SHALL maintain sufficient color contrast ratios for readability.\n* Normal text SHALL meet WCAG 2.1 AA minimum contrast ratio of 4.5:1.\n* Large text (18pt+) SHALL meet minimum contrast ratio of 3:1.\n* Contrast requirements SHALL be met in both dark and light themes.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_044] - Blog Platform  Color Contrast Test #BP044\n* **Objective:** Verify WCAG 2.1 AA color contrast compliance.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Run Lighthouse accessibility audit (dark theme)  Expect no contrast failures\n  - TC2: Run Lighthouse accessibility audit (light theme)  Expect no contrast failures\n  - TC3: Check body text contrast  Expect 4.5:1 ratio\n  - TC4: Check heading contrast  Expect 4.5:1 for normal, 3:1 for large\n  - TC5: Check link contrast  Expect distinguishable from surrounding text\n  - TC6: Check code block contrast  Expect readable in both themes\n* **Tools:** axe DevTools, WAVE, Colour Contrast Analyser\n* **Manual Check:** Verify UI is readable for color-blind users\n\nREQ: [BP045] - Blog Platform  Logical Reading Order #N051\n* Rendered HTML SHALL maintain logical reading order when CSS is disabled.\n* Content sequence SHALL be meaningful without visual styling.\n* Navigation, main content, and footer SHALL appear in expected order.\n* Content SHALL NOT rely on CSS for meaning or sequence.\n\nQA: [BP_QA_045] - Blog Platform  Reading Order Test #BP045\n* **Objective:** Verify logical content order without CSS.\n* **Test Cases:**\n  - TC1: Disable CSS in browser  Expect content still readable\n  - TC2: Read page top-to-bottom  Expect logical sequence\n  - TC3: Verify navigation position  Expect before main content\n  - TC4: Verify main content  Expect after navigation\n  - TC5: Verify footer position  Expect at end of document\n  - TC6: Test with screen reader  Expect announces in correct order\n* **Source Order:** Inspect HTML source order matches visual layout intent\n* **CLI Browser:** Verify reading order in lynx matches expected flow\n\nREQ: [BP046] -
